## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear oscillator ODEs. Common models combine a restoring force term f(x), damping term g(v,x)*v, and optional external/parametric forcing h(t,x).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (small-amplitude linear spring)
- Linear viscous damping + linear spring: dv_dt = -c0 * v + -c1 * x (damped harmonic oscillator)
- Constant bias / gravity-like offset: dv_dt = c0 + -c1 * x + -c2 * v (equilibrium shifted by constant acceleration)
- Cubic Duffing restoring (hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * x**3 (nonlinear stiffness; conservative if no v-term)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v + -c1 * x + -c2 * x**3 (nonlinear spring with viscous losses)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = -c0 * x + -c1 * x**3 + -c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring nonlinearity)
- Quadratic / turbulent drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v) + -c1 * x (velocity-squared dissipation at higher Reynolds number)
- Nonlinear damping depending on displacement: dv_dt = -c0 * (c1 + x**2) * v + -c2 * x (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 + -x**2) * v + -c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 + -v**2) * v + -c2 * x (nonlinear damping in v, self-sustained oscillations)
- Driven oscillator (additive periodic forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * v + -c1 * x + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external sinusoidal drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * v + -c1 * x + -c2 * x**3 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/bi-stability regimes)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -c0 * v + -(c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * x (time-periodic stiffness, parametric resonance)
- General potential-force form: dv_dt = -c0 * v + -(c1 * x + c2 * x**3 + c3 * x**5) (restoring as polynomial gradient of potential plus damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force тЖТ dv_dt depends on x only (no v, no explicit t); often an odd function in x for symmetric potentials (e.g., -x, -x - x**3).
- Hardening vs softening stiffness тЖТ positive vs negative coefficient on x**3 in the restoring term changes frequencyтАУamplitude dependence and can create multi-stability when combined with forcing.
- Viscous losses тЖТ a term proportional to -v yields exponential energy decay; adding x-dependent prefactors (-(a+x**2)*v) makes damping amplitude-dependent.
- Aerodynamic/turbulent dissipation тЖТ -v*Abs(v) produces stronger damping at large speeds and non-exponential ring-down.
- Self-excited oscillations (limit cycles) тЖТ damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (1-x**2)*v or (1-v**2)*v, injects energy at small amplitude and removes it at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing тЖТ additive cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms create resonance peaks, entrainment, and (with nonlinearity) hysteresis/jumps.
- Parametric forcing тЖТ stiffness modulation via (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x leads to instability tongues (Mathieu behavior) even without additive drive.
- Symmetry breaking / shifted equilibria тЖТ constant terms in dv_dt or even-in-x restoring terms (e.g., x**2) shift equilibrium and introduce waveform asymmetry.
- Time-invariance check тЖТ if dv_dt shows no explicit t-dependence, prefer autonomous forms dv_dt=f(x,v); explicit t suggests drive/parametric excitation or time-varying parameters.
